<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_154632144">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154632144" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/665907-aileen" class="left imgcol" title="Aileen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1291271811p2/665907.jpg" alt="Aileen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/154632144?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/665907-aileen" class="user" title="Aileen">Aileen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/26054.The_MacGregors" title="Paperback 9780373285136" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/665907-aileen?shelf=creepy" class="actionLinkLite">creepy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/665907-aileen?shelf=smutty" class="actionLinkLite">smutty</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/665907-aileen?shelf=double-you-tee-eff-mate" class="actionLinkLite">double-you-tee-eff-mate</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154632144">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2883919528521303659">Flannery and I were talking about my latest status update and what to do to possibly fix this. Our interchange went as thus:<br /><br /> F: Well, what have you been reading?<br />A: I dunno, I read halfway through the first MacGregor book but I had to stop because it was so bad.<br />F: What do you mean? I remember kind of liking it. And plus, Nora Roberts! Can't be that bad, right?<br />A: It was so bad that I looked up when it was published to see if it was written earlier in her career.<br />(Some discussion about the formattin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2883919528521303659">Flannery and I were talking about my latest status update and what to do to possibly fix this. Our interchange went as thus:<br /><br /> F: Well, what have you been reading?<br />A: I dunno, I read halfway through the first MacGregor book but I had to stop because it was so bad.<br />F: What do you mean? I remember kind of liking it. And plus, Nora Roberts! Can't be that bad, right?<br />A: It was so bad that I looked up when it was published to see if it was written earlier in her career.<br />(Some discussion about the formatting of the ebook being the possible culprit, which I'll omit for boringness' sake.)<br />F: What was so bad about it?<br /><br />Well, first off, the guy's name is Justin Blade and he's a gambler on a boat. Granted, it's not a steamboat and we're not in the 1800s, but all I could visualize from that point forward was:<br /><br /><img width="300" height="648" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347028i/701359._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><em>Not really that appealing</em><br /><br />Secondly, Justin's seduction of Serena went a lot like this:<br />J: You want me (kisses Serena forcibly).<br />S: No, I don't! (shoves him away ineffectually)<br />J: ...or dooo youuuuu??? (kisses Serena forcibly)<br />S: Nooo. (Leans into him while thinking about how much she wants to do him.)<br /><br />I have a few problems with this scenario: (1) I read this during the reading and emotional stress of our Rape Cases in Criminal Law. I read multiple cases about women who were afraid to come forward to talk about their experience because they were afraid no one would believe them. I got really mad at Serena because she's a consenting adult and had the capacity to say yes, but kept saying no for what, to prove a point? Say no when you mean no, chica, and stop devaluing the term with your trite protestations. (2) Justin's a jerk. No amount of "But (dramatic pause) I LOVE YOU" that eventually comes later on in the book overrides the fact that he's an overbearing jerk. (3) There's a lot of "Oh you lovable scamp you, Serena" with metaphorical sighs and proud smiles whenever Serena does something annoying. She's not cute, she's annoying. I know you're fictional characters, but that's shoddy parenting skills, MacGregors.<br /><br />I gave this two stars because I didn't finish the second story in the book. I could eventually finish the book, but not in the near future. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2883919528521303659">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_62733411">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62733411" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1411916-bonnie" class="left imgcol" title="Bonnie"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Bonnie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62733411?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 08, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1411916-bonnie" class="user" title="Bonnie">Bonnie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/26054.The_MacGregors" title="Paperback 9780373285136" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62733411">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5767448838885282166">Both of these books start out with the strong-willed heroine being "unwilling" to fall in love with the main dude. The main dude basically stalks the girl- sending her gifts after repeatedly being asked not to, showing up around them, arranging things so that they'll be bound by business, "forcefully kissing" her even after she's said no, and so on- wearing her down until, apparently, sheer animal lust or something takes over, and then she realizes that not only is this dude hot, he's perfect fo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5767448838885282166">Both of these books start out with the strong-willed heroine being "unwilling" to fall in love with the main dude. The main dude basically stalks the girl- sending her gifts after repeatedly being asked not to, showing up around them, arranging things so that they'll be bound by business, "forcefully kissing" her even after she's said no, and so on- wearing her down until, apparently, sheer animal lust or something takes over, and then she realizes that not only is this dude hot, he's perfect for her. So, basically- the guy acts like a creepy asshole stalker/rapist/circa 1950s male until she realizes that her own dreams and ideas and reasons for not being with him are nothing compared to his ultimate hotness. Normally I think pretty highly of Nora Roberts- one of my faves for the genre- but I can't stand yet another of these "stalker wins" books. MacGregors = fail.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5767448838885282166">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_425116929">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425116929" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10762842-nicole" class="left imgcol" title="Nicole"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1341687158p2/10762842.jpg" alt="Nicole" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/425116929?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 30, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10762842-nicole" class="user" title="Nicole">Nicole</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/26054.The_MacGregors" title="Paperback 9780373285136" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer425116929">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer582780930547111158">I am quickly learning that the early romance version of my favorite author is a mere <em>silhouette</em> of the best-selling powerhouse she has become.<br /><br />Serena and Caine MacGregor are the youngest children of the great Daniel MacGregor - a modern-day Scottish lord that rules over his family with never-ending love and a hope that they all find the love he has known with his wife and children...even if that involves a bit of heavy-handed meddling! In the case of Serena and Caine, their potential true loves c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText582780930547111158">I am quickly learning that the early romance version of my favorite author is a mere <em>silhouette</em> of the best-selling powerhouse she has become.<br /><br />Serena and Caine MacGregor are the youngest children of the great Daniel MacGregor - a modern-day Scottish lord that rules over his family with never-ending love and a hope that they all find the love he has known with his wife and children...even if that involves a bit of heavy-handed meddling! In the case of Serena and Caine, their potential true loves come in the duo of Justin and Diana Blade - estranged siblings of Comanche descent who always fight for what they want and prefer to gamble when the odds are in their favor.<br /><br />This book lives up the expectations incurred from the <em>Silhoutte</em> reputation: love at first sight, flash-point passion, and happily-ever-after....and some truly yummy leading men! ;) I am far from conservative and greatly enjoy books that have a couple tumbles in the sheets, but I also like a semblance of a plot and development of relationships that are external to the primary love interest - both of which are lacking in this book even though there was lots of potential for both. Because the two stories are contained in one double volume, it is even more painfully obvious that they were written from a "mad-lib" romance format and many of the same phrases were used in each!<br /><br />I actually don't place too much of the blame on NR, I have a feeling that <em> Silhouette </em> doesn't branch too far from the formulaic romance plot with lots of steamy overtones. It does make me have a lot more appreciation for NR's newer works, which demonstrate that great romance novels can actually be much more complex than simple bodice-ripping and can actually be <em>enhanced</em> by well-written secondary characters. I will forever recommend Nora Roberts books to others but, unless you are a true fan of the old-school romance style of writing, I would steer clear of the <em>Silhouette</em> editions.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="582780930547111158">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1139648078237513611">Er bestaat werkelijk voor alles een eerste keer. Dus bestaat er jammer genoeg ook een Nora Roberts-boek dat me niet wist te overtuigen. ‘Serena en Cain’, het tweede boek uit deze ‘De MacGregor Clan’-reeks bestaat uit twee korte verhalen waarin de jongste zus Serena en één van haar beide broers de hoofdrol voor rekening nemen.<br /><br />Jammer genoeg wist geen één van beide verhalen me echt te overhalen.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText1139648078237513611">Er bestaat werkelijk voor alles een eerste keer. Dus bestaat er jammer genoeg ook een Nora Roberts-boek dat me niet wist te overtuigen. ‘Serena en Cain’, het tweede boek uit deze ‘De MacGregor Clan’-reeks bestaat uit twee korte verhalen waarin de jongste zus Serena en één van haar beide broers de hoofdrol voor rekening nemen.<br /><br />Jammer genoeg wist geen één van beide verhalen me echt te overhalen. Dit boek werd oorspronkelijk gepubliceerd in 1985 en dat merk je. Als lezer viel het me duidelijk op dat een boek dertig jaar geleden letterlijk én figuurlijk een heel ander verhaal was. De schrijfstijl, de uitdrukkingen, het gedrag en de verwachtingen van personages … Bovendien hebben die karakters ook nog eens de gewoonte om vrijwel continu het ene te zeggen terwijl ze het tegenovergestelde bedoelen. Op een bepaald moment begrijpt een van niet wat iemand probeert uit te leggen, maar wanneer een ander personage het twee minuten later op dezelfde manier uitlegt klinkt het hem plots wel logisch in de oren.<br /><br />...<br /><br />Mijn volledige recensie kan je <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.zwartraafje.be/blog/2015/01/serena-en-cain-nora-roberts/"> hier </a> terugvinden.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17195171359314527626">I really like Serena and Justin's story-the cruise and hotel/casino setting and both their sassiness...great love story and the skillet won the day haha! Now when it came to Caine and Diana...I really tried but I've to admit: I do not like Diana.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText17195171359314527626">I really like Serena and Justin's story-the cruise and hotel/casino setting and both their sassiness...great love story and the skillet won the day haha! Now when it came to Caine and Diana...I really tried but I've to admit: I do not like Diana. I first read about her in Ian's story and liked her...but when I saw her in Grant's story I did not quite expect her "difficult-ness"...her being so cool to Gennie and then not telling Caine she's pregnant. ..I have read the stories backwards and was kinda looking forward to see just how bad her childhood was to make her the way she is. Sad to say I think she's a wimp...I know she's supposed to be gutsy to have quit her cushy job and rebelled against the cold and mean aunt, but she really was the nastiest to Caine who gave her so much room to be herself! The way she blamed Caine the morning aft the blizzard...then she felt sorry and wanted to apologise but cos she was so hungry she decided no way she's going to say sorry...and Caine was spot on when he accused her of not being able to trust him and always throwing his ladies'man rep in his face. If she served up 10% of the nastiness to her aunt growing up maybe she won't be so screwed up. She made it thru law school and it never occurred to her to maybe try to search for her bro? No I do not like Diana the character.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17195171359314527626">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13878317312981326624">Daniel's romantic machinations embroil Serena and Caine with another brother and sister team, Justin and Diana Blade. In Playing the Odds, Comanche gambler Justin Blade finds himself on a vacation cruise to the Bahamas where he is instantly attracted to a violet-eyed casino dealer. Only later does he learn that the lissome Serena is one and the same as the much-degreed Rena MacGregor, daughter of his longtime silent business partner, Daniel MacGregor. Serena makes it her practice to never get in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13878317312981326624">Daniel's romantic machinations embroil Serena and Caine with another brother and sister team, Justin and Diana Blade. In Playing the Odds, Comanche gambler Justin Blade finds himself on a vacation cruise to the Bahamas where he is instantly attracted to a violet-eyed casino dealer. Only later does he learn that the lissome Serena is one and the same as the much-degreed Rena MacGregor, daughter of his longtime silent business partner, Daniel MacGregor. Serena makes it her practice to never get involved with gamblers, but the predatory gaze of Justin Blade steals her breath and steels her resolve to ignore his overtures. When Justin makes her an offer she can't refuse--the position of casino manager in his Atlantic City hotel-casino--Serena finds herself drawn to the man who worked his way up from nowhere, never swerving in his pursuit of financial success and possession of Serena. In this contemporary drama, the house (and the heart) always wins! Once settled as Justin's partner in business and in life, Serena invites Justin's sister Diana to visit. To Diana, Justin is the beloved older brother who abandoned her 20 years earlier, after their mother's death, leaving Diana to be raised by her cold Aunt Adelaide who demanded absolute obedience from her. Now a Harvard-educated lawyer in Boston, Diana is a cool operator, her emotions packed tightly away, until Caine MacGregor, her new sister-in-law's brother and infamous rogue of Harvard Law's ivied halls, greets her at the airport on her visit to get to know the brother she loved so long ago. Diana finds herself in turmoil, trying to deal with her hurt and anger toward her brother and the attraction that she feels for Caine who just happens to be near whenever Diana's well-guarded shell cracks. Caine works inexorably to overcome the much-exaggerated tales of his law school peccadilloes, slowly changing Diana's mind about his playboy reputation and teaching her to trust her heart and him.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3453693527220084677">okay,so there's two seperate books in this book-typical nora fashion-so i'll start with Playing the Odds.it was funny in places, which i love in books.<br />when i first started reading romance book i found the attitude like Justin Blade's charming-likeable,even,but now i find myself not having any warm feelings-i am most certainly not <span id="freeTextContainer4823191512994710723">Fourth and fifth in the MacGregor romance series. Read <a target="_blank" title="Opens Nora Roberts' Playing the Odds in Goodreads" href="http://www.goodreads.com/book/show/490609.Playing_The_Odds">a review I did earlier</a> on this particular story.<br /><br /><strong> <em>Tempting Fates</em> </strong> finds Diana meeting her brother again for the first time in two decades where she learns some unpalata</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4823191512994710723">Fourth and fifth in the MacGregor romance series.     <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_264964482">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264964482" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/715656-christi-snow" class="left imgcol" title="Christi Snow"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442626986p2/715656.jpg" alt="Christi Snow" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/264964482?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 20, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/715656-christi-snow" class="user" title="Christi Snow">Christi Snow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8599629-serena-caine" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780373281336" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer264964482">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10914688641831981216">This book is a re-release of two of Nora Roberts books featuring the MacGregor family from 1985. Whoa, it's been a long time since I read anything written this long ago. I forgot how corny some of the romantic scenes could be. Between that and societal changes...lots of sexual harassment, smoking indoors, mentions of typewriters and telegrams. It was kind of fun to revisit this older style of romance. And quite honestly, beyond the corniness and the cliche conflicts, I did enjoy reading both of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10914688641831981216">This book is a re-release of two of Nora Roberts books featuring the MacGregor family from 1985. Whoa, it's been a long time since I read anything written this long ago. I forgot how corny some of the romantic scenes could be. Between that and societal changes...lots of sexual harassment, smoking indoors, mentions of typewriters and telegrams. It was kind of fun to revisit this older style of romance. And quite honestly, beyond the corniness and the cliche conflicts, I did enjoy reading both of these stories.<br /><br /><br />Playing the Odds<br />Serena &amp; Justin<br /><br />Story Overview:<br />Serena MacGregor had been looking for a little independence and some much-needed adventure, but Justin Blade was not what she had in mind. The stakes were high, and Justin was betting on changing Serena's mind about him. But when this fiery heiress upped the ante on the cool Comanche gambler, steamy didn't begin to describe the results.?<br /><br />My Rating: B-<br /><br />My Review:<br />Daniel MacGregor is the patriarch of the MacGregor clan. He has mentored Justin for 10 years, but in that time, Justin has never met Rena, Daniel's daughter. When Daniel convinces Justin to take a vacation cruise, Justin doesn't think anything of it. As a professional gambler, he is immediately enchanted with a female dealer who works on the ship, Serena. Unbeknownst to either of them, they have been set up by Daniel to meet.<br /><br />In this book, the cruise ship made the book. I am not a huge fan of books based around gambling, but I loved the ambience provided by the ship and the exotic ports of call. I enjoyed the MacGregor family clan and the story line of Justin's past. These books are based around family and the family dynamics were defined and highlighted very early so that you realize how important the family ties are to the overall story. I liked that. Justin had a HORRIBLE childhood, so that makes it so that he appreciates the MacGregors all that much more.<br /><br />Overall, this was entertaining. I was just sad at how dated it did feel. The cheeseball lines during the sex scenes did provide some fun giggles though....<br /><br /><br /><br />Tempting Fate<br />Caine &amp; Diana<br /><br />Story Overview:<br />Attorney Caine MacGregor had a reputation for being a demon in and out of the courtroom. The dashing young attorney rarely met a case—or a woman—he couldn't win. But Diana Blade was no ordinary lady. Caine yearned to break down her icy wall of control and release the passionate woman within. He might be able to convince Diana to form a business partnership, but could he entice her to risk everything for the love of a MacGregor?<br /><br />My Rating: B<br /><br />My Review:<br />For me, this book seemed to have a bit more depth than the first. Diana is Hunter's (hero from the first book) younger sister. When their parents died, he abandoned her to a harsh, strict aunt and Diana basically grew up without knowing any love in her life. That has left her with HUGE scars when it comes to relationships. She has been ruled with an iron fist by her aunt her entire life. Now that she is out on her own and able to make her own decisions, she NEVER plans to open herself up to someone else. She never wants to give anyone else ANY power over her life OR the ability to leave and hurt her like her entire family did when she was little.<br /><br />The flip side of that is Caine who has always had a very easy time with women, so when Diana turns him down, he is hurt and devastated. There is a lot of emotion in this book. And again, this is a book that shows its era because there is a LOT of sexual harassment in it too. One minute Caine will be attacking Diana and telling her that he is going to bed her...it's a guarantee. Then the next minute, he's trying to forge a work relationship. It was almost funny how unacceptable that would be now. No woman in her right mind would give a guy like that ANY leeway in her life....personal or professional. We have definitely changed in the last 27 years.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10914688641831981216">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5334103989824648455">The first story within this book was with Serena McGregor and Justin Blade. I have to honestly say I was throughly please and enjoyed reading this book. It kept you wanting to read more and was edgy because of the kidnapping and the darkend past behind Justin Blade's character. It was well written and I have to say my favorite character is her boisterous father! I just loved how he demanded grandchildren for the mother's sake and how he played match maker in both books. The second story was a little more subdued than the first. The second book was with Caine McGregor (Brother of Serena McGregor) and Diana Blade (Sister of Justin Blade). This book was whimsical and romantic with touches of reality and distress. It was a great read and once again my favorite character was the escentric father, with his cigars and scottish burrs you can't help but to fall in love with how lively his character is. This book is part of a series and I can't wait to see what the other McGregors have in store. Nora Roberts once again wrote a book that I love and will remember. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11141411299879236086">I love this book. I love the MacGregor family.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText11141411299879236086">I love this book. I love the MacGregor family. Daniel MacGregor’s first matchmaking attempt for his daughter, Serena and his young friend Justin is hilarious. It cracks me up with both find out that Daniel planned them meeting. Playing the Odds was very funny and heartwarming. When Serena is kidnapped later on in the story, and when Justin is able to admit his love for her, it makes me think of the miracle of love, and it makes me want to hug them both when Justin rushes to save her--- and she has saved herself. She is no damsel in distress, and that makes me love her character even more. I love when Diana Blade’s cool façade is cracked when she meets and fall in love with Caine. It is so amazing how similar they are (both lawyers who with to Harvard) and it cracks me up when Diana reminds Caine of his exploits that are still bandied about the halls and dorms of Harvard. He tries to explain that they are exaggerated. The first two children of Daniel MacGregor are amazing and funny. I would recommend this book to lovers of romance and Nora Roberts.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4158590471482523145">"The MacGregors:Serena &amp; Caine" was thoroughly enjoyable. In Nora Roberts's style, the book is part of a family series and consists of 2 stories-- "Playing the Odds" tells the story of Serena and "Tempting Fate" tells the story of her brother Caine. Prominently behind the scenes is Daniel MacGregor, patriarch of the MacGregor family, who only wants the best for his children. Other characters in these stories are Justin Blade- half Comanche Indian and owner of multiple casinos and his sister,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4158590471482523145">"The MacGregors:Serena &amp; Caine" was thoroughly enjoyable. In Nora Roberts's style, the book is part of a family series and consists of 2 stories-- "Playing the Odds" tells the story of Serena and "Tempting Fate" tells the story of her brother Caine. Prominently behind the scenes is Daniel MacGregor, patriarch of the MacGregor family, who only wants the best for his children. Other characters in these stories are Justin Blade- half Comanche Indian and owner of multiple casinos and his sister, Diana, who hasn't seen him for 20 years. I'm anxious to read the rest of the books in this series and meet other members of this family. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17225480647970048779">There really isn't any surprise or literary merit to this book, but it did make a quick and easy read. It is obvious that the two main characters of both of the books will end up together and that there will be some sort of conflict to complicate matters. I only had two objections about the two books. The first being that the father, Daniel was a very singular and to be quite honest a very creepy character. He keeps mentioning that his children should reproduce in terms that liken it to animals</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17225480647970048779">There really isn't any surprise or literary merit to this book, but it did make a quick and easy read. It is obvious that the two main characters of both of the books will end up together and that there will be some sort of conflict to complicate matters. I only had two objections about the two books. The first being that the father, Daniel was a very singular and to be quite honest a very creepy character. He keeps mentioning that his children should reproduce in terms that liken it to animals breeding. Not a characteristic I would want in a father. The other objection has to be that the male love interests in their "desire" for their female counterparts basically come close to rape. The way that it is described, these men don't seem romantic, but rather two people who could be put in prison for sexual assault. Aside from that, I would recommend this to people that have some free-time to fill with two fluffy romance stories. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17225480647970048779">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16583788616430007555">I loved these stories by Nora Roberts.<br /><br />Playing the odds<br /><br />I loved this story about Serena and Justin. I loved the tension and passion that flared between the two. I loved that they were brought together by Serenas matchmaking dad, Daniel who thought they were perfect for each other. With a bomb threat and kidnapping it became a great book that i struggled to put down. cannot wait to continue into the series. <br /><br />Tempting Fate<br /><br />I loved this story about Caine and Diana but did not enjoy it as much as the fi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16583788616430007555">I loved these stories by Nora Roberts.<br /><br />Playing the odds<br /><br />I loved this story about Serena and Justin. I loved the tension and passion that flared between the two. I loved that they were brought together by Serenas matchmaking dad, Daniel who thought they were perfect for each other. With a bomb threat and kidnapping it became a great book that i struggled to put down. cannot wait to continue into the series. <br /><br />Tempting Fate<br /><br />I loved this story about Caine and Diana but did not enjoy it as much as the first story. Both of them are lawyers and are brought together when Diana comes to meet her brother. They then fall in love but insecurities get in the way. I loved following their story but I did find it disappointing that we didn't see more of Diana's and Justin's relationship forming. It was still a great story and cannot wait to continue in the series.<br /><br />Definitely a series I would recommend. Xxxx</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <a href="/user/show/8443209-elizabeth" class="user" title="Elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer359732443">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2622018052267667249">For Serena and Caine, I liked these stories.<br /><br />I guess my only complaint is that all the stories follow the same outline, they find their match, push them away, have mind blowing sex, still don't let them in, and because one of the character's is just "that much more hear headed" than the other, they wind up together, to continue on with a happy ending.<br /><br />It's in the little details, and the way that Daniel commands the children to visit their mother, which is very touching. All of them know that it is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2622018052267667249">For Serena and Caine, I liked these stories.<br /><br />I guess my only complaint is that all the stories follow the same outline, they find their match, push them away, have mind blowing sex, still don't let them in, and because one of the character's is just "that much more hear headed" than the other, they wind up together, to continue on with a happy ending.<br /><br />It's in the little details, and the way that Daniel commands the children to visit their mother, which is very touching. All of them know that it is he who misses his children, but is too pride filled to admit it.<br /><br />I still enjoyed the series, even though I knew the pattern, which was very similar to the "Calhoun" series.<br /><br />Very fast stories to read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2622018052267667249">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8047446051456141073">3.5 stars: Great beach read<br /><br />I really like this light hearted, laugh out loud series. Great characters. Endearing and hard to put down. I've read most of the books in this series and enjoyed them all. Not knowing it was a series, I started with MagGregor Brides (the one with the MacGregor acting as matchmaker for his grandaughters). It was hiliarous. I was hooked. <br /><br />My favs in the series are the later books with three generations of MacGregors and the matchmaking, meddlesome grandfather. I actually think I liked the series more by starting with those books, because it made me more interested to go back and read the other characters story. Also I loved the way the MacGregor was protrayed.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11289157343182174946">I really like the MacGregors series.. but for some reason, Serena and Caine's story didn't have that "umph", if you know what I mean..<br /><br />Actually, it was nice but it kind of fell into the traditional love story of love stories. It was a good read without being boring but also without being exciting.<br /><br />In a scale of "omg, i can't put this book down because i'm so hooked" of 1-10 with 10 being the highest, I'd say it's somewhere around 4. It was something I liked but also something I can do without finishing it immediately. There are books that when you read them, you just can't put it down. I have not experienced that with this one.<br /><br />Oh well, at least they had a happy ending ;)</span>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts">About Nora Roberts</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts"><img alt="625" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1440685355p2/625.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer8687434458975582710">Nora Roberts was born in Silver Spring, Maryland. She began writing when a blizzard in February 1979 kept her in her hilltop home with a three and six year old for nearly a week of canceled kindergarten and dwindling chocolate supplies. <br /><br />During the now-famous blizzard, she pulled out a pencil and notebook and began to write a story for her own entertainment. From the first page, she knew it was wha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8687434458975582710">Nora Roberts was born in Silver Spring, Maryland. She began writing when a blizzard in February 1979 kept her in her hilltop home with a three and six year old for nearly a week of canceled kindergarten and dwindling chocolate supplies. <br /><br />During the now-famous blizzard, she pulled out a pencil and notebook and began to write a story for her own entertainment. From the first page, she knew it was what she was meant to do. Several manuscripts and rejections later, Irish Thoroughbred was published by Silhouette in 1981.<br /><br />The Liar, published in April 2015 by Putnam, is her 214th book. She hit the NY Times Bestseller list in 1991. Every book since 1999 has made that list.<br /><br />Recently The New Yorker called her “America’s favorite novelist."<br /><br />In 1995, she began writing a police procedural series featuring Eve Dallas, a NY homicide cop, and set in the near future under the J.D. Robb pseudonym. Devoted in Death, out in September 2015, is the 41st entry in the series.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8687434458975582710">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Nora Roberts...</a>
